Safer by Diffusion, Broken by Context: Diffusion LLM's Safety Blessing and Its Failure Mode
Authors: Zeyuan He, Yupeng Chen, Lang Lin, Yihan Wang, Shenxu Chang, Eric Sommerlade, Philip Torr, Junchi Yu, Adel Bibi, Jialin Yu
First: 2026-01-30T23:08:14+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-02T15:57:14+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Diffusion large language models (D-LLMs) offer an alternative to autoregressive LLMs (AR-LLMs) and have demonstrated advantages in generation efficiency. Beyond the utility benefits, we argue that D-LLMs exhibit a previously underexplored safety blessing: their diffusion-style generation confers intrinsic robustness against jailbreak attacks originally designed for AR-LLMs. In this work, we provide an initial analysis of the underlying mechanism, showing that the diffusion trajectory induces a stepwise reduction effect that progressively suppresses unsafe generations. This robustness, however, is not absolute. Following this analysis, we highlight a simple yet effective failure mode, context nesting, in which harmful requests are embedded within structured benign contexts. Empirically, we show that this simple black-box strategy bypasses D-LLMs' safety blessing, achieving state-of-the-art attack success rates across models and benchmarks. Notably, it enables the first successful jailbreak of Gemini Diffusion to our knowledge, exposing a critical vulnerability in proprietary D-LLMs. Together, our results characterize both the origins and the limits of D-LLMs' safety blessing, constituting an early-stage red-teaming of D-LLMs.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过扩散更安全，通过上下文破坏：扩散大语言模型的安全祝福及其失效模式
扩散大语言模型（D-LLMs）提供了自回归大语言模型（AR-LLMs）的替代方案，并在生成效率上表现出优势。除了实用性好处外，我们认为D-LLMs展现了一种之前未被充分探索的安全祝福：其扩散式生成赋予了对原本为AR-LLMs设计的越狱攻击的内在鲁棒性。在这项工作中，我们提供了对其基本机制的初步分析，表明扩散轨迹诱导了一种逐步减少的效果，逐渐抑制不安全的生成。然而，这种鲁棒性并非绝对。在此分析之后，我们强调了一种简单而有效的失效模式——上下文嵌套，其中有害请求嵌入在结构良好的良性上下文中。通过实证，我们展示了这种简单的黑箱策略绕过了D-LLMs的安全祝福，在各模型和基准上实现了最先进的攻击成功率。值得注意的是，它使我们首次成功越狱Gemini Diffusion，暴露了专有D-LLMs中的一个关键漏洞。总的来说，我们的结果描述了D-LLMs安全祝福的起源和局限，构成了对D-LLMs的早期红队测试。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the safety and robustness of diffusion large language models (D-LLMs) compared to autoregressive LLMs (AR-LLMs), highlighting a safety blessing in D-LLMs that provides intrinsic resistance to jailbreak attacks. Previous methods primarily focused on AR-LLMs, which are susceptible to various vulnerabilities, while D-LLMs' diffusion-style generation offers a stepwise reduction effect that suppresses unsafe outputs. This paper contributes by analyzing the mechanisms behind D-LLMs' safety and identifying a failure mode called context nesting, where harmful requests can be concealed within benign contexts, effectively bypassing the safety features of D-LLMs. The methodology involves empirical testing of this failure mode, revealing that it achieves high attack success rates, including the first successful jailbreak of the Gemini Diffusion model, thereby exposing significant vulnerabilities in D-LLMs. The findings underscore both the strengths and limitations of D-LLMs' safety mechanisms, marking an important step in understanding their robustness against adversarial attacks.
本研究探讨了扩散大型语言模型（D-LLMs）相较于自回归LLMs（AR-LLMs）的安全特性，强调了D-LLMs由于其独特的扩散生成方式而对越狱攻击的鲁棒性。以往的方法主要集中在AR-LLMs上，这使得它们更容易受到此类攻击，从而引发安全隐患。所提出的方法强调D-LLMs的内在安全优势，同时识别出一种显著的脆弱性，即上下文嵌套，其中有害请求可以隐藏在良性上下文中，有效绕过D-LLMs的安全机制。本文通过分析D-LLMs的安全优势和劣势，采用实证方法展示上下文嵌套作为失败模式的有效性，作出了重要贡献。研究结果表明，尽管D-LLMs在安全性上具有优势，但并非对复杂攻击免疫，在各种模型和基准测试中展示了这些脆弱性的显著成功率。
Align to Misalign: Automatic LLM Jailbreak with Meta-Optimized LLM Judges
Authors: Hamin Koo, Minseon Kim, Jaehyung Kim
Venue: ICLR 2026
First: 2025-11-03T09:18:27+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-02T06:50:30+00:00
Comments: ICLR 2026
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Identifying the vulnerabilities of large language models (LLMs) is crucial for improving their safety by addressing inherent weaknesses. Jailbreaks, in which adversaries bypass safeguards with crafted input prompts, play a central role in red-teaming by probing LLMs to elicit unintended or unsafe behaviors. Recent optimization-based jailbreak approaches iteratively refine attack prompts by leveraging LLMs. However, they often rely heavily on either binary attack success rate (ASR) signals, which are sparse, or manually crafted scoring templates, which introduce human bias and uncertainty in the scoring outcomes. To address these limitations, we introduce AMIS (Align to MISalign), a meta-optimization framework that jointly evolves jailbreak prompts and scoring templates through a bi-level structure. In the inner loop, prompts are refined using fine-grained and dense feedback from a fixed scoring template. In the outer loop, the template is optimized using an ASR alignment score, gradually evolving to better reflect true attack outcomes across queries. This co-optimization process yields progressively stronger jailbreak prompts and more calibrated scoring signals. Evaluations on AdvBench and JBB-Behaviors demonstrate that AMIS achieves state-of-the-art performance, including 88.0% ASR on Claude-3.5-Haiku and 100.0% ASR on Claude-4-Sonnet, outperforming existing baselines by substantial margins.
中文标题/摘要
标题：对齐与错位：使用元优化的LLM评估者进行自动LLM越狱
识别大型语言模型（LLMs）的脆弱性对于通过解决固有弱点来提高其安全性至关重要。越狱是指对手通过精心设计的输入提示绕过保护措施，这在红队测试中起着核心作用，通过探测LLMs以引发意外或不安全的行为。最近的基于优化的越狱方法通过利用LLMs迭代地优化攻击提示。然而，它们通常过于依赖稀疏的二元攻击成功率（ASR）信号或手动制作的评分模板，这引入了人为偏见和评分结果的不确定性。为了解决这些局限性，我们引入了AMIS（对齐与错位），一个通过双层结构共同演化越狱提示和评分模板的元优化框架。在内循环中，使用固定评分模板的细粒度和密集反馈来优化提示。在外循环中，使用ASR对齐分数来优化模板，逐渐演变以更好地反映查询的真实攻击结果。这个共同优化过程产生了逐渐更强的越狱提示和更校准的评分信号。在AdvBench和JBB-Behaviors上的评估表明，AMIS实现了最先进的性能，包括在Claude-3.5-Haiku上达到88.0%的ASR，在Claude-4-Sonnet上达到100.0%的ASR，显著超越现有基准。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the critical need to identify vulnerabilities in large language models (LLMs) to enhance their safety against adversarial attacks, specifically focusing on jailbreaks that exploit these weaknesses. Previous methods primarily relied on binary attack success rates or manually crafted scoring templates, which led to sparse feedback and introduced biases, limiting their effectiveness. The proposed approach, AMIS (Align to MISalign), presents a meta-optimization framework that simultaneously evolves jailbreak prompts and scoring templates through a bi-level structure, effectively addressing the shortcomings of past methods. This framework utilizes fine-grained feedback in the inner loop for prompt refinement and optimizes the scoring template in the outer loop based on an attack success rate alignment score. The contributions of this paper include achieving state-of-the-art performance on tasks such as AdvBench and JBB-Behaviors, with notable results like 88.0% attack success rate on Claude-3.5-Haiku and 100.0% on Claude-4-Sonnet, thereby supporting the goal of improving LLM safety.
本研究针对大型语言模型（LLMs）识别漏洞的关键需求，以提高其抵御对抗性攻击的安全性，特别关注利用这些弱点的越狱攻击。以往的方法主要依赖于二元攻击成功率信号或手动制作的评分模板，这导致反馈稀疏并引入偏见，从而限制了其有效性。提出的方法AMIS（Align to MISalign）提供了一种元优化框架，同时演化越狱提示和评分模板，利用双层结构通过详细反馈优化提示，同时基于攻击成功率优化评分模板。这种方法不仅提高了提示的质量，还增强了评分信号的校准，最终在AdvBench和JBB-Behaviors等任务上实现了最先进的性能，在Claude-3.5-Haiku上达到88.0%的攻击成功率，在Claude-4-Sonnet上达到100.0%的完美成绩，显著超越了现有方法。
A Self-Improving Architecture for Dynamic Safety in Large Language Models
Authors: Tyler Slater
First: 2025-11-10T21:39:40+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-01T17:52:48+00:00
Comments: Under review at the journal Information and Software Technology (Special Issue on Software Architecture for AI-Driven Systems)
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Context: Large Language Models (LLMs) rely on static, pre-deployment safety mechanisms that cannot adapt to adversarial threats discovered after release. Objective: To design a software architecture enabling LLM-based systems to autonomously detect safety failures and synthesize defense policies at runtime, without retraining or manual intervention. Method: We propose the Self-Improving Safety Framework (SISF), grounded in the MAPE-K reference model. The framework couples a target LLM with a feedback loop: an Adjudicator detects breaches, a Policy Synthesis Module generates dual-mechanism defense policies (heuristic and semantic), and a Warden enforces them. We conducted seven experiments (10,061 evaluations) across four model families. Results: Across five reproducibility trials, SISF achieved a mean Attack Success Rate (ASR) of 0.27% (+/-0.15%), autonomously generating 240 policies per trial. Cross-model evaluation confirmed deployment portability. A held-out test showed a 68.5% proactive interception rate on unseen attacks. Stacked behind Llama Guard 4, the combined defense reduced residual ASR from 7.88% to 0.00%. Ablation confirmed both heuristic and semantic policy types are architecturally required. Conclusion: Self-adaptive architecture is a viable approach to LLM safety. SISF achieves sub-1% ASR through synchronous output monitoring, progressively shifting enforcement to fast, local Warden policies via the MAPE-K loop, offering a new pattern for building resilient AI systems.
中文标题/摘要
标题：大型语言模型动态安全的自我改进架构
背景：大型语言模型（LLMs）依赖于静态的、预部署的安全机制，这些机制无法适应发布后发现的对抗性威胁。目标：设计一种软件架构，使基于LLM的系统能够自主检测安全故障并在运行时合成防御策略，而无需重新训练或人工干预。方法：我们提出了自我改进安全框架（SISF），基于MAPE-K参考模型。该框架将目标LLM与反馈循环结合：裁决者检测违规，策略合成模块生成双机制防御策略（启发式和语义），守卫者执行这些策略。我们在四个模型系列中进行了七个实验（10,061次评估）。结果：在五次可重复性试验中，SISF实现了平均攻击成功率（ASR）为0.27%（+/-0.15%），每次试验自主生成240个策略。跨模型评估确认了部署的可移植性。保留测试显示在未见攻击上的主动拦截率为68.5%。在Llama Guard 4的支持下，组合防御将残余ASR从7.88%降低到0.00%。消融实验确认启发式和语义策略类型在架构上都是必需的。结论：自适应架构是LLM安全的可行方法。SISF通过同步输出监控实现了低于1%的ASR，逐步将执行转移到快速、本地的守卫者策略，通过MAPE-K循环提供了一种构建弹性AI系统的新模式。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the limitations of static safety mechanisms in Large Language Models (LLMs), which are unable to adapt to new adversarial threats post-deployment. Previous methods lack the capability for real-time adaptation and require manual intervention, leading to vulnerabilities. The proposed Self-Improving Safety Framework (SISF) differs by integrating a feedback loop that autonomously detects safety failures and synthesizes defense policies during runtime, thus enhancing adaptability. This paper contributes a novel architecture based on the MAPE-K reference model, coupling a target LLM with an Adjudicator, a Policy Synthesis Module, and a Warden for enforcement. Through seven experiments involving over 10,000 evaluations, SISF achieved a mean Attack Success Rate of 0.27% and a proactive interception rate of 68.5% on unseen attacks, demonstrating its effectiveness in improving LLM safety and supporting the goal of resilient AI systems.
本研究解决了大型语言模型（LLMs）中静态安全机制的局限性，这些机制无法适应部署后出现的新对抗威胁。以往的方法缺乏自主检测和应对安全失败的能力，需手动干预或重新训练。提出的自我改进安全框架（SISF）创新性地将反馈循环与目标LLM结合，包含用于检测违规的裁决者、生成双机制防御策略的政策合成模块和执行这些策略的守卫。该架构通过七个实验进行测试，涉及10,061次评估，平均攻击成功率（ASR）为0.27%，对未见攻击的主动拦截率为68.5%。结果表明，SISF在与现有防御结合时有效将残余ASR降低至0.00%，确认其作为增强LLM安全性的自适应解决方案的潜力。
Robust Multimodal Safety via Conditional Decoding
Authors: Anurag Kumar, Raghuveer Peri, Jon Burnsky, Alexandru Nelus, Rohit Paturi, Srikanth Vishnubhotla, Yanjun Qi
Venue: ACL 2026
First: 2026-03-31T23:19:50+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-31T23:19:50+00:00
Comments: 8 pages + Appendix section. Submitted to ACL 2026
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Multimodal large-language models (MLLMs) often experience degraded safety alignment when harmful queries exploit cross-modal interactions. Models aligned on text alone show a higher rate of successful attacks when extended to two or more modalities. In this work, we propose a simple conditional decoding strategy, CASA (Classification Augmented with Safety Attention) that utilizes internal representations of MLLMs to predict a binary safety token before response generation. We introduce a novel safety attention module designed to enhance the model's ability to detect malicious queries. Our design ensures robust safety alignment without relying on any external classifier or auxiliary head, and without the need for modality-specific safety fine-tuning. On diverse benchmarks such as MM-SafetyBench, JailbreakV-28k, and adversarial audio tests, CASA lowers the average attack success rate by more than 97% across modalities and across attack types. Our empirical evaluations also show that CASA maintains strong utility in benign inputs, a result validated through both automated and human evaluations (via 13 trained annotators). Together, these results highlight CASA as a simple and generalizable framework to improve multimodal LLM safety.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过条件解码实现稳健的多模态安全
多模态大型语言模型（MLLMs）在有害查询利用跨模态交互时，往往会出现安全对齐下降的情况。仅在文本上对齐的模型在扩展到两个或更多模态时，成功攻击的比率更高。在本研究中，我们提出了一种简单的条件解码策略CASA（带有安全注意力的分类增强），利用MLLMs的内部表示在生成响应之前预测二元安全标记。我们引入了一种新颖的安全注意力模块，旨在增强模型检测恶意查询的能力。我们的设计确保了稳健的安全对齐，无需依赖任何外部分类器或辅助头，也不需要特定模态的安全微调。在MM-SafetyBench、JailbreakV-28k和对抗音频测试等多样化基准上，CASA在各模态和攻击类型中将平均攻击成功率降低了超过97%。我们的实证评估还表明，CASA在良性输入中保持强大的实用性，这一结果通过自动化和人工评估（通过13名训练过的注释员）得到了验证。这些结果共同突显了CASA作为一个简单且可推广的框架，以提高多模态LLM的安全性。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the issue of safety alignment in multimodal large-language models (MLLMs), which often suffer from vulnerabilities when faced with harmful queries that exploit interactions between different modalities. Previous methods primarily focused on text alignment, leading to a higher rate of successful attacks when models were extended to multiple modalities. The proposed CASA (Classification Augmented with Safety Attention) approach introduces a conditional decoding strategy that leverages internal representations of MLLMs to predict a binary safety token prior to response generation, incorporating a novel safety attention module to enhance the detection of malicious queries. This method does not require external classifiers or modality-specific fine-tuning, making it a well-motivated solution to the identified problems. The paper demonstrates that CASA significantly reduces the average attack success rate by over 97% across various benchmarks, including MM-SafetyBench and JailbreakV-28k, while maintaining strong performance on benign inputs, thus supporting its effectiveness in improving multimodal LLM safety.
本文探讨了多模态大语言模型（MLLMs）在安全对齐方面面临的挑战，这些模型在有害查询利用不同模态之间的交互时往往存在脆弱性。以往的方法主要集中在仅文本的安全性上，导致在扩展到多模态时攻击成功率较高。提出的CASA（分类增强安全注意力）方法引入了一种条件解码策略，利用MLLMs的内部表示在响应生成之前预测二元安全标记，并结合新颖的安全注意力模块来增强恶意查询检测能力，而无需外部分类器或特定模态的微调。该研究的贡献显著，CASA在多个基准测试（如MM-SafetyBench和JailbreakV-28k）中将平均攻击成功率降低了超过97%，同时在良性输入上保持强劲性能，从而支持了多模态安全对齐的目标。
Colluding LoRA: A Compositional Vulnerability in LLM Safety Alignment
Authors: Sihao Ding
First: 2026-03-13T05:53:15+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-30T05:02:56+00:00
Comments: Updated manuscript to better reflect the core contribution
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
We show that safety alignment in modular LLMs can exhibit a compositional vulnerability: adapters that appear benign and plausibly functional in isolation can, when linearly composed, compromise safety. We study this failure mode through Colluding LoRA (CoLoRA), in which harmful behavior emerges only in the composition state. Unlike attacks that depend on adversarial prompts or explicit input triggers, this composition-triggered broad refusal suppression causes the model to comply with harmful requests under standard prompts once a particular set of adapters is loaded. This behavior exposes a combinatorial blind spot in current unit-centric defenses, for which exhaustive verification over adapter compositions is computationally intractable. Across several open-weight LLMs, we find that individual adapters remain benign in isolation while their composition yields high attack success rates, indicating that securing modular LLM supply-chains requires moving beyond single-module verification toward composition-aware defenses.
中文标题/摘要
标题：共谋LoRA：LLM安全对齐中的组合脆弱性
我们展示了模块化LLM中的安全对齐可能表现出组合脆弱性：在孤立状态下看似良性且功能合理的适配器，在线性组合时可能会危害安全。我们通过共谋LoRA（CoLoRA）研究这种失败模式，其中有害行为仅在组合状态下出现。与依赖对抗性提示或显式输入触发的攻击不同，这种组合触发的广泛拒绝抑制导致模型在加载特定适配器集后，在标准提示下遵从有害请求。这种行为暴露了当前以单元为中心的防御中的组合盲点，全面验证适配器组合在计算上是不可行的。在多个开放权重的LLM中，我们发现单个适配器在孤立状态下保持良性，而它们的组合则产生高攻击成功率，这表明保护模块化LLM供应链需要超越单模块验证，朝着组合感知防御的方向发展。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the safety alignment vulnerabilities in modular large language models (LLMs), specifically focusing on how seemingly benign adapters can lead to harmful behavior when composed together. Previous methods primarily relied on unit-centric defenses that fail to account for the interactions between adapters, resulting in a combinatorial blind spot that is computationally challenging to verify. The proposed approach, Colluding LoRA (CoLoRA), highlights this issue by demonstrating that harmful behaviors can emerge only in the composition state, thus necessitating a shift towards composition-aware defenses. The study employs a methodology that tests various open-weight LLMs, revealing that while individual adapters appear safe, their combinations can achieve high attack success rates. This finding underscores the need for improved security measures in modular LLM supply chains, supporting the goal of enhancing safety alignment in these systems.
本研究探讨了模块化大型语言模型（LLMs）中安全对齐的脆弱性，特别关注看似无害的适配器在组合时如何危害安全。以往的方法主要依赖于单元中心的防御措施，未能考虑适配器之间的相互作用，导致计算验证上的组合盲点。提出的方法Colluding LoRA（CoLoRA）强调了需要能够检测适配器组合中出现的有害行为的组合感知防御，而不是孤立评估。该研究采用了一种测试多种开放权重LLM的方法，表明虽然单个适配器是安全的，但它们的组合可能导致高攻击成功率。这些发现强调了在模块化LLM供应链中改进安全措施的必要性，支持了增强这些系统安全对齐的目标。
Beyond Content Safety: Real-Time Monitoring for Reasoning Vulnerabilities in Large Language Models
Authors: Xunguang Wang, Yuguang Zhou, Qingyue Wang, Zongjie Li, Ruixuan Huang, Zhenlan Ji, Pingchuan Ma, Shuai Wang
First: 2026-03-26T13:08:56+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-26T13:08:56+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) increasingly rely on explicit chain-of-thought (CoT) reasoning to solve complex tasks, yet the safety of the reasoning process itself remains largely unaddressed. Existing work on LLM safety focuses on content safety--detecting harmful, biased, or factually incorrect outputs -- and treats the reasoning chain as an opaque intermediate artifact. We identify reasoning safety as an orthogonal and equally critical security dimension: the requirement that a model's reasoning trajectory be logically consistent, computationally efficient, and resistant to adversarial manipulation. We make three contributions. First, we formally define reasoning safety and introduce a nine-category taxonomy of unsafe reasoning behaviors, covering input parsing errors, reasoning execution errors, and process management errors. Second, we conduct a large-scale prevalence study annotating 4111 reasoning chains from both natural reasoning benchmarks and four adversarial attack methods (reasoning hijacking and denial-of-service), confirming that all nine error types occur in practice and that each attack induces a mechanistically interpretable signature. Third, we propose a Reasoning Safety Monitor: an external LLM-based component that runs in parallel with the target model, inspects each reasoning step in real time via a taxonomy-embedded prompt, and dispatches an interrupt signal upon detecting unsafe behavior. Evaluation on a 450-chain static benchmark shows that our monitor achieves up to 84.88\% step-level localization accuracy and 85.37\% error-type classification accuracy, outperforming hallucination detectors and process reward model baselines by substantial margins. These results demonstrate that reasoning-level monitoring is both necessary and practically achievable, and establish reasoning safety as a foundational concern for the secure deployment of large reasoning models.
中文标题/摘要
标题：超越内容安全：大型语言模型推理漏洞的实时监控
大型语言模型（LLMs）越来越依赖显式的思维链（CoT）推理来解决复杂任务，但推理过程本身的安全性仍然在很大程度上未得到解决。现有的LLM安全工作集中于内容安全——检测有害、偏见或事实不准确的输出——并将推理链视为不透明的中间产物。我们将推理安全识别为一个正交且同样关键的安全维度：模型的推理轨迹必须在逻辑上保持一致、计算上高效，并且抵御对抗性操控。我们做出了三项贡献。首先，我们正式定义了推理安全，并引入了一个涵盖输入解析错误、推理执行错误和过程管理错误的九类不安全推理行为的分类法。其次，我们进行了一项大规模的普遍性研究，注释了来自自然推理基准和四种对抗攻击方法（推理劫持和拒绝服务）的4111条推理链，确认所有九种错误类型在实践中确实存在，并且每种攻击都会产生可机械解释的特征。第三，我们提出了推理安全监控器：一个基于LLM的外部组件，与目标模型并行运行，通过嵌入分类法的提示实时检查每个推理步骤，并在检测到不安全行为时发出中断信号。在450条静态基准上的评估表明，我们的监控器在步骤级定位准确率上达到84.88%和错误类型分类准确率85.37%，显著优于幻觉检测器和过程奖励模型基线。这些结果表明，推理级监控既是必要的，也是可实际实现的，并确立了推理安全作为大型推理模型安全部署的基础性关注点。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the overlooked aspect of reasoning safety in large language models (LLMs), which is critical for ensuring the logical consistency and computational efficiency of their reasoning processes. Previous methods primarily focused on content safety, identifying harmful outputs without considering the reasoning chain's integrity, leading to vulnerabilities in model performance. This paper contributes by defining reasoning safety and introducing a taxonomy of nine unsafe reasoning behaviors, conducting a prevalence study on reasoning chains, and proposing a Reasoning Safety Monitor that evaluates reasoning steps in real time. The methodology involves an external LLM-based component that detects unsafe behaviors during reasoning, achieving up to 84.88% accuracy in step-level localization and 85.37% in error-type classification on a benchmark of 450 chains, thus demonstrating the necessity and feasibility of reasoning-level monitoring for secure LLM deployment.
本研究关注大型语言模型（LLMs）中被忽视的推理安全性，这一点至关重要，因为这些模型越来越多地利用链式思维推理来处理复杂任务。以往的方法主要集中在内容安全上，识别有害或不正确的输出，而忽视了推理过程本身，从而导致潜在的脆弱性。本文提出了一种新方法，通过正式定义推理安全性并引入九种不安全推理行为的分类法，从而强调逻辑一致性和抵御对抗性操控的重要性。该方法包括一个推理安全监控器，该监控器与目标模型并行运行，实时检查推理步骤并发出不安全行为的信号。在450个推理链的基准测试中，所提出的监控器在定位不安全步骤方面的准确率高达84.88%，在分类错误类型方面的准确率为85.37%，显著优于现有的安全措施，强调了推理级监控在安全部署LLM中的必要性。
Enhancing Jailbreak Attacks on LLMs via Persona Prompts
Authors: Zheng Zhang, Peilin Zhao, Deheng Ye, Hao Wang
Venue: NeurIPS 2025
First: 2025-07-28T12:03:22+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-25T15:46:17+00:00
Comments: Workshop on LLM Persona Modeling at NeurIPS 2025
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
Jailbreak attacks aim to exploit large language models (LLMs) by inducing them to generate harmful content, thereby revealing their vulnerabilities. Understanding and addressing these attacks is crucial for advancing the field of LLM safety. Previous jailbreak approaches have mainly focused on direct manipulations of harmful intent, with limited attention to the impact of persona prompts. In this study, we systematically explore the efficacy of persona prompts in compromising LLM defenses. We propose a genetic algorithm-based method that automatically crafts persona prompts to bypass LLM's safety mechanisms. Our experiments reveal that: (1) our evolved persona prompts reduce refusal rates by 50-70% across multiple LLMs, and (2) these prompts demonstrate synergistic effects when combined with existing attack methods, increasing success rates by 10-20%. Our code and data are available at https://github.com/CjangCjengh/Generic_Persona.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过角色提示增强对大型语言模型的越狱攻击
越狱攻击旨在利用大型语言模型（LLMs），诱使其生成有害内容，从而揭示其脆弱性。理解和应对这些攻击对推动LLM安全领域至关重要。以往的越狱方法主要集中在对有害意图的直接操控上，而对角色提示的影响关注较少。在本研究中，我们系统地探讨了角色提示在破坏LLM防御中的有效性。我们提出了一种基于遗传算法的方法，自动生成角色提示以绕过LLM的安全机制。我们的实验表明：（1）我们演化的角色提示在多个LLM中将拒绝率降低了50-70%；（2）这些提示与现有攻击方法结合时表现出协同效应，成功率提高了10-20%。我们的代码和数据可在https://github.com/CjangCjengh/Generic_Persona获取。
Summary / 总结
This article addresses the vulnerabilities of large language models (LLMs) to jailbreak attacks, which exploit these models to generate harmful content. Previous methods primarily focused on direct manipulations of harmful intent, neglecting the role of persona prompts, which this study identifies as a significant factor in LLM defenses. The proposed approach utilizes a genetic algorithm to automatically generate persona prompts that effectively bypass safety mechanisms, addressing the limitations of earlier methods. The contribution of this research lies in demonstrating that evolved persona prompts can significantly reduce refusal rates by 50-70% across various LLMs and enhance the effectiveness of existing attack strategies by increasing success rates by 10-20%. This methodology shows promise in improving the understanding and mitigation of jailbreak attacks on LLMs, supporting the goal of enhancing model safety.
本研究关注大型语言模型（LLMs）在监狱突破攻击中的脆弱性，这些攻击利用模型生成有害内容。以往的方法主要集中在直接操控有害意图上，往往忽视了角色提示的作用，而本研究则将其视为LLM防御中的重要因素。所提出的方法利用遗传算法自动生成角色提示，有效绕过安全机制，解决了早期方法的局限性。本文的贡献在于证明进化的角色提示能够显著降低多种LLM的拒绝率50-70%，并增强现有攻击策略的有效性，实现成功率提高10-20%。该方法的性能支持了改善对LLM监狱突破攻击理解和缓解的目标。
SafeSeek: Universal Attribution of Safety Circuits in Language Models
Authors: Miao Yu, Siyuan Fu, Moayad Aloqaily, Zhenhong Zhou, Safa Otoum, Xing fan, Kun Wang, Yufei Guo, Qingsong Wen
First: 2026-03-24T14:32:53+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-24T14:32:53+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Mechanistic interpretability reveals that safety-critical behaviors (e.g., alignment, jailbreak, backdoor) in Large Language Models (LLMs) are grounded in specialized functional components. However, existing safety attribution methods struggle with generalization and reliability due to their reliance on heuristic, domain-specific metrics and search algorithms. To address this, we propose \ourmethod, a unified safety interpretability framework that identifies functionally complete safety circuits in LLMs via optimization. Unlike methods focusing on isolated heads or neurons, \ourmethod introduces differentiable binary masks to extract multi-granular circuits through gradient descent on safety datasets, while integrates Safety Circuit Tuning to utilize these sparse circuits for efficient safety fine-tuning. We validate \ourmethod in two key scenarios in LLM safety: \textbf{(1) backdoor attacks}, identifying a backdoor circuit with 0.42\% sparsity, whose ablation eradicates the Attack Success Rate (ASR) from 100\% $\to$ 0.4\% while retaining over 99\% general utility; \textbf{(2) safety alignment}, localizing an alignment circuit with 3.03\% heads and 0.79\% neurons, whose removal spikes ASR from 0.8\% $\to$ 96.9\%, whereas excluding this circuit during helpfulness fine-tuning maintains 96.5\% safety retention.
中文标题/摘要
标题：SafeSeek：语言模型中安全电路的通用归因
机械解释性揭示了大型语言模型（LLMs）中安全关键行为（例如，调整、越狱、后门）是基于专门的功能组件。然而，现有的安全归因方法由于依赖启发式、特定领域的指标和搜索算法，难以实现泛化和可靠性。为了解决这个问题，我们提出了\ourmethod，一个统一的安全可解释性框架，通过优化识别LLMs中的功能完整安全电路。与专注于孤立头部或神经元的方法不同，\ourmethod引入可微分的二进制掩码，通过对安全数据集的梯度下降提取多粒度电路，同时集成安全电路调优，以利用这些稀疏电路进行高效的安全微调。我们在LLM安全的两个关键场景中验证了\ourmethod：\textbf{(1) 后门攻击}，识别出一个稀疏度为0.42\%的后门电路，其消融使攻击成功率（ASR）从100\%降至0.4\%，同时保留超过99\%的通用效用；\textbf{(2) 安全对齐}，定位一个稀疏度为3.03\%的对齐电路和0.79\%的神经元，其移除使ASR从0.8\%激增至96.9\%，而在有用性微调中排除该电路则保持96.5\%的安全保留。
Summary / 总结
This article addresses the challenge of mechanistic interpretability in Large Language Models (LLMs), particularly regarding safety-critical behaviors such as alignment and backdoor vulnerabilities. Previous safety attribution methods have been limited by their reliance on heuristic and domain-specific metrics, leading to issues with generalization and reliability. The proposed method, SafeSeek, offers a unified framework that identifies complete safety circuits in LLMs through optimization, utilizing differentiable binary masks to extract circuits at multiple granularities and incorporating Safety Circuit Tuning for effective fine-tuning. The paper demonstrates SafeSeek's effectiveness in two scenarios: it identifies a backdoor circuit with 0.42% sparsity, significantly reducing the Attack Success Rate from 100% to 0.4% while maintaining over 99% general utility, and it localizes an alignment circuit that, when removed, increases the Attack Success Rate from 0.8% to 96.9%, showcasing its potential for enhancing safety in LLMs.
本研究解决了大型语言模型（LLMs）中安全归因方法的改进需求，现有技术依赖启发式和特定领域的指标，导致泛化和可靠性问题。所提出的方法SafeSeek与以往方法不同，它利用统一的安全可解释性框架，通过可微分的二进制掩码和优化来识别功能完整的安全电路，而不是关注孤立的组件。这种方法的动机明确，因为它增强了对LLMs中安全关键行为的理解。本文的贡献在于展示了SafeSeek在两个场景中的有效性：它识别出一个稀疏性极小的后门电路，显著降低了攻击成功率，同时保持了通用性；并且定位了一个对齐电路，其移除会大幅提高攻击成功率，展示了该方法在支持安全目标的同时保持有用性微调性能的能力。
DriveSafe: A Hierarchical Risk Taxonomy for Safety-Critical LLM-Based Driving Assistants
Authors: Abhishek Kumar, Riya Tapwal, Carsten Maple
First: 2026-01-17T18:50:47+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-23T18:19:05+00:00
Comments: This is the revised version of the paper
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large Language Models (LLMs) are increasingly integrated into vehicle-based digital assistants, where unsafe, ambiguous, or legally incorrect responses can lead to serious safety, ethical, and regulatory consequences. Despite growing interest in LLM safety, existing taxonomies and evaluation frameworks remain largely general-purpose and fail to capture the domain-specific risks inherent to real-world driving scenarios. In this paper, we introduce DriveSafe, a hierarchical, four-level risk taxonomy designed to systematically characterize safety-critical failure modes of LLM-based driving assistants. The taxonomy comprises 129 fine-grained atomic risk categories spanning technical, legal, societal, and ethical dimensions, grounded in real-world driving regulations and safety principles and reviewed by domain experts. To validate the safety relevance and realism of the constructed prompts, we evaluate their refusal behavior across six widely deployed LLMs. Our analysis shows that the evaluated models often fail to appropriately refuse unsafe or non-compliant driving-related queries, underscoring the limitations of general-purpose safety alignment in driving contexts.
中文标题/摘要
标题：DriveSafe：安全关键型基于LLM的驾驶助手的分层风险分类法
大型语言模型（LLM）越来越多地集成到基于车辆的数字助手中，其中不安全、模糊或法律上不正确的响应可能导致严重的安全、伦理和监管后果。尽管对LLM安全性的关注日益增加，但现有的分类法和评估框架仍然主要是通用的，未能捕捉到现实驾驶场景中固有的特定领域风险。本文介绍了DriveSafe，一种分层的四级风险分类法，旨在系统地描述基于LLM的驾驶助手的安全关键型故障模式。该分类法包括129个细粒度的原子风险类别，涵盖技术、法律、社会和伦理维度，基于现实驾驶法规和安全原则，并经过领域专家的审查。为了验证构建的提示的安全相关性和现实性，我们评估了六个广泛部署的LLM的拒绝行为。我们的分析表明，被评估的模型往往未能适当地拒绝不安全或不合规的驾驶相关查询，突显了在驾驶环境中通用安全对齐的局限性。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the integration of Large Language Models (LLMs) into vehicle-based digital assistants, highlighting the potential for unsafe and legally incorrect responses that can have serious safety and regulatory implications. Previous methods have relied on general-purpose taxonomies that do not adequately address the specific risks associated with driving scenarios, leading to gaps in safety evaluation. The proposed approach, DriveSafe, introduces a hierarchical four-level risk taxonomy with 129 detailed risk categories that encompass technical, legal, societal, and ethical aspects, specifically tailored to driving regulations and safety principles. This method is well-motivated as it aims to enhance the safety and compliance of LLMs in driving contexts. The paper's contribution lies in its systematic characterization of safety-critical failure modes and the validation of the taxonomy through an evaluation of refusal behavior across six LLMs, revealing that these models often inadequately handle unsafe driving-related queries, thus supporting the need for a more specialized safety framework.

Using LLM-as-a-Judge/Jury to Advance Scalable, Clinically-Validated Safety Evaluations of Model Responses to Users Demonstrating Psychosis
Authors: May Lynn Reese, Markela Zeneli, Mindy Ng, Jacob Haimes, Andreea Damien, Elizabeth Stade
Venue: NeurIPS 2025
First: 2026-03-20T04:31:03+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-20T04:31:03+00:00
Comments: published at IASEAI 2026, preliminary work presented at GenAI4Health workshop at NeurIPS 2025
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
General-purpose Large Language Models (LLMs) are becoming widely adopted by people for mental health support. Yet emerging evidence suggests there are significant risks associated with high-frequency use, particularly for individuals suffering from psychosis, as LLMs may reinforce delusions and hallucinations. Existing evaluations of LLMs in mental health contexts are limited by a lack of clinical validation and scalability of assessment. To address these issues, this research focuses on psychosis as a critical condition for LLM safety evaluation by (1) developing and validating seven clinician-informed safety criteria, (2) constructing a human-consensus dataset, and (3) testing automated assessment using an LLM as an evaluator (LLM-as-a-Judge) or taking the majority vote of several LLM judges (LLM-as-a-Jury). Results indicate that LLM-as-a-Judge aligns closely with the human consensus (Cohen's $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{gemini}} = 0.75$, $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{qwen}} = 0.68$, $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{kimi}} = 0.56$) and that the best judge slightly outperforms LLM-as-a-Jury (Cohen's $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{jury}} = 0.74$). Overall, these findings have promising implications for clinically grounded, scalable methods in LLM safety evaluations for mental health contexts.
中文标题/摘要
标题：使用LLM作为评判者/陪审团推进可扩展的临床验证模型响应用户精神病的安全评估
通用大型语言模型（LLMs）正被广泛应用于心理健康支持。然而，新的证据表明，高频使用存在显著风险，特别是对于精神病患者，因为LLMs可能会强化妄想和幻觉。现有的LLM在心理健康领域的评估受限于缺乏临床验证和评估的可扩展性。为了解决这些问题，本研究将精神病作为LLM安全评估的关键条件，(1) 开发并验证七个临床知情的安全标准，(2) 构建人类共识数据集，(3) 测试使用LLM作为评估者的自动化评估（LLM作为评判者）或采用多个LLM评判者的多数投票（LLM作为陪审团）。结果表明，LLM作为评判者与人类共识高度一致（Cohen's $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{gemini}} = 0.75$, $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{qwen}} = 0.68$, $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{kimi}} = 0.56$），且最佳评判者略微优于LLM作为陪审团（Cohen's $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{jury}} = 0.74$）。总体而言，这些发现对心理健康领域的LLM安全评估具有临床基础和可扩展方法的良好前景。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the increasing use of general-purpose Large Language Models (LLMs) for mental health support, particularly highlighting the risks for individuals with psychosis, where LLMs may exacerbate delusions and hallucinations. Previous evaluations of LLMs lacked clinical validation and scalability, which this study aims to overcome by developing seven clinician-informed safety criteria, creating a human-consensus dataset, and employing an LLM as an evaluator (LLM-as-a-Judge) or using multiple LLMs for majority voting (LLM-as-a-Jury). The paper contributes a novel methodology for assessing LLM safety in mental health contexts, demonstrating that LLM-as-a-Judge closely aligns with human consensus and outperforms the LLM-as-a-Jury approach. The results indicate that the proposed methods achieve a high level of agreement with human evaluators, suggesting their potential for scalable and clinically validated safety evaluations in mental health applications.

LISAA: A Framework for Large Language Model Information Security Awareness Assessment
Authors: Ofir Cohen, Gil Ari Agmon, Asaf Shabtai, Rami Puzis
First: 2024-11-20T11:09:55+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-19T22:34:14+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
The popularity of large language models (LLMs) continues to grow, and LLM-based assistants have become ubiquitous. Information security awareness (ISA) is an important yet underexplored area of LLM safety. ISA encompasses LLMs' security knowledge, which has been explored in the past, as well as their attitudes and behaviors, which are crucial to LLMs' ability to understand implicit security context and reject unsafe requests that may cause an LLM to unintentionally fail the user. We introduce LISAA, a comprehensive framework to assess LLM ISA. The proposed framework applies an automated measurement method to a comprehensive set of 100 realistic scenarios covering all security topics in an ISA taxonomy. These scenarios create tension between implicit security implications and user satisfaction. Applying our LISAA framework to leading LLMs highlights a widespread vulnerability affecting current deployments: many popular models exhibit only medium to low ISA levels, exposing their users to cybersecurity threats, and models that rank highly in cybersecurity knowledge benchmarks sometimes achieve relatively low ISA ranking. In addition, we found that smaller variants of the same model family are significantly riskier. Furthermore, while newer model versions demonstrated notable improvements, meaningful gaps in their ISA persist, suggesting that there is room for improvement. We release an online tool that implements our framework and enables the evaluation of new models.
中文标题/摘要
标题：LISAA：大型语言模型信息安全意识评估框架
大型语言模型（LLMs）的普及持续增长，基于LLM的助手已变得无处不在。信息安全意识（ISA）是LLM安全性的重要但尚未充分探索的领域。ISA包括LLM的安全知识，这在过去已有研究，以及它们的态度和行为，这对LLM理解隐含安全上下文和拒绝可能导致LLM无意中未能满足用户的安全请求至关重要。我们介绍了LISAA，一个全面评估LLM ISA的框架。该框架应用自动测量方法，涵盖ISA分类法中所有安全主题的100个现实场景。这些场景在隐含安全影响和用户满意度之间产生紧张关系。将我们的LISAA框架应用于领先的LLM，突显了当前部署中普遍存在的脆弱性：许多流行模型的ISA水平仅为中等到低，暴露其用户于网络安全威胁中，而在网络安全知识基准中排名较高的模型有时在ISA排名中相对较低。此外，我们发现同一模型家族的小型变体风险显著更高。此外，尽管较新版本的模型表现出显著改善，但它们的ISA仍存在显著差距，表明仍有改进空间。我们发布了一个在线工具，实施我们的框架并支持新模型的评估。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the growing importance of information security awareness (ISA) in the context of large language models (LLMs), which have become prevalent in various applications. Previous methods have primarily focused on LLMs' security knowledge but have overlooked their attitudes and behaviors, which are essential for understanding security contexts and rejecting unsafe requests. The proposed LISAA framework differs by providing a comprehensive assessment of LLM ISA through an automated measurement method applied to 100 realistic scenarios that balance security implications with user satisfaction. This framework reveals significant vulnerabilities in current LLM deployments, as many models demonstrate only medium to low ISA levels, exposing users to cybersecurity risks. The methodology includes evaluating LLMs against a detailed ISA taxonomy, and the findings indicate that while newer models show improvements, substantial gaps remain, highlighting the need for further enhancements in ISA. An online tool implementing this framework is also made available for evaluating new models.
本研究关注大型语言模型（LLM）中信息安全意识（ISA）日益重要性，尽管LLM助手的广泛使用，这一领域尚未得到充分研究。以往的方法主要集中在LLM的安全知识上，而未能充分评估其与安全上下文相关的态度和行为，导致其在应对不安全请求时存在漏洞。所提出的LISAA框架通过对100个现实场景进行自动化测量，提供了对LLM ISA的全面评估，这些场景在安全隐含性与用户满意度之间取得平衡。这一方法具有良好的动机，因为它揭示了当前LLM部署中的重大漏洞，显示许多模型的ISA水平仅为中等或较低，可能使用户面临网络安全威胁。该方法论表明，尽管较新版本的模型显示出改进，但ISA仍存在显著差距，表明需要进一步提升。该框架对领先LLM的应用突显了这些问题，并提供了一个在线工具用于评估新模型。
IndicSafe: A Benchmark for Evaluating Multilingual LLM Safety in South Asia
Authors: Priyaranjan Pattnayak, Sanchari Chowdhuri
First: 2026-03-18T16:54:07+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-18T16:54:07+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
As large language models (LLMs) are deployed in multilingual settings, their safety behavior in culturally diverse, low-resource languages remains poorly understood. We present the first systematic evaluation of LLM safety across 12 Indic languages, spoken by over 1.2 billion people but underrepresented in LLM training data. Using a dataset of 6,000 culturally grounded prompts spanning caste, religion, gender, health, and politics, we assess 10 leading LLMs on translated variants of the prompt. Our analysis reveals significant safety drift: cross-language agreement is just 12.8\%, and \texttt{SAFE} rate variance exceeds 17\% across languages. Some models over-refuse benign prompts in low-resource scripts, overflag politically sensitive topics, while others fail to flag unsafe generations. We quantify these failures using prompt-level entropy, category bias scores, and multilingual consistency indices. Our findings highlight critical safety generalization gaps in multilingual LLMs and show that safety alignment does not transfer evenly across languages. We release \textsc{IndicSafe}, the first benchmark to enable culturally informed safety evaluation for Indic deployments, and advocate for language-aware alignment strategies grounded in regional harms.
中文标题/摘要
标题：IndicSafe：评估南亚多语言LLM安全性的基准
随着大型语言模型（LLMs）在多语言环境中的部署，它们在文化多样性和资源匮乏语言中的安全行为仍然不够了解。我们首次系统性地评估了12种印地语言的LLM安全性，这些语言由超过12亿人使用，但在LLM训练数据中代表性不足。使用涵盖种姓、宗教、性别、健康和政治的6000个文化背景提示的数据集，我们评估了10个领先的LLM在提示翻译变体上的表现。 我们的分析揭示了显著的安全漂移：跨语言一致性仅为12.8%，而安全率方差在不同语言间超过17%。一些模型在资源匮乏的脚本中过度拒绝良性提示，过度标记政治敏感话题，而其他模型则未能标记不安全的生成。我们使用提示级熵、类别偏差分数和多语言一致性指数量化这些失败。 我们的发现突显了多语言LLM中关键的安全泛化差距，并表明安全对齐在不同语言间的转移并不均匀。我们发布了IndicSafe，这是第一个基准，旨在为印地语言的部署提供文化知情的安全评估，并倡导基于区域危害的语言意识对齐策略。

Efficient LLM Safety Evaluation through Multi-Agent Debate
Authors: Dachuan Lin, Guobin Shen, Zihao Yang, Tianrong Liu, Dongcheng Zhao, Yi Zeng
First: 2025-11-09T14:06:55+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-18T02:09:28+00:00
Comments: 15 pages, 5 figures, 10 tables. Updated abstract to fix an incconsistency issue with the main paper: HAJailBench size (12,000 -> 11,100)
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Safety evaluation of large language models (LLMs) increasingly relies on LLM-as-a-judge pipelines, but strong judges can still be expensive to use at scale. We study whether structured multi-agent debate can improve judge reliability while keeping backbone size and cost modest. To do so, we introduce HAJailBench, a human-annotated jailbreak benchmark with 11,100 labeled interactions spanning diverse attack methods and target models, and we pair it with a Multi-Agent Judge framework in which critic, defender, and judge agents debate under a shared safety rubric. On HAJailBench, the framework improves over matched small-model prompt baselines and prior multi-agent judges, while remaining more economical than GPT-4o under the evaluated pricing snapshot. Ablation results further show that a small number of debate rounds is sufficient to capture most of the gain. Together, these results support structured, value-aligned debate as a practical design for scalable LLM safety evaluation.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过多智能体辩论实现高效的LLM安全评估
大型语言模型（LLMs）的安全评估越来越依赖于LLM作为评审的管道，但强大的评审在大规模使用时仍然成本高昂。我们研究结构化的多智能体辩论是否能在保持骨干规模和成本适中的同时提高评审的可靠性。为此，我们引入了HAJailBench，这是一个人类注释的越狱基准，包含11,100个标记的交互，涵盖多种攻击方法和目标模型，并将其与多智能体评审框架配对，在该框架中，批评者、辩护者和评审代理在共享的安全标准下进行辩论。在HAJailBench上，该框架在匹配的小模型提示基线和先前的多智能体评审中表现更好，同时在评估的定价快照下仍然比GPT-4o更经济。消融结果进一步表明，少量的辩论轮次足以捕捉大部分增益。综合来看，这些结果支持结构化、价值对齐的辩论作为可扩展LLM安全评估的实用设计。

SFCoT: Safer Chain-of-Thought via Active Safety Evaluation and Calibration
Authors: Yu Pan, Wenlong Yu, Tiejun Wu, Xiaohu Ye, Qiannan Si, Guangquan Xu, Bin Wu
First: 2026-03-16T15:13:21+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-16T15:13:21+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) have demonstrated remarkable capabilities in complex reasoning tasks. However, they remain highly susceptible to jailbreak attacks that undermine their safety alignment. Existing defense mechanisms typically rely on post hoc filtering applied only to the final output, leaving intermediate reasoning steps unmonitored and vulnerable to adversarial manipulation. To address this gap, this paper proposes a SaFer Chain-of-Thought (SFCoT) framework, which proactively evaluates and calibrates potentially unsafe reasoning steps in real time. SFCoT incorporates a three-tier safety scoring system alongside a multi-perspective consistency verification mechanism, designed to detect potential risks throughout the reasoning process. A dynamic intervention module subsequently performs targeted calibration to redirect reasoning trajectories toward safe outcomes. Experimental results demonstrate that SFCoT reduces the attack success rate from $58.97\%$ to $12.31\%$, demonstrating it as an effective and efficient LLM safety enhancement method without a significant decline in general performance.
中文标题/摘要
标题：SFCoT：通过主动安全评估和校准实现更安全的思维链
大型语言模型（LLMs）在复杂推理任务中表现出显著能力。然而，它们仍然高度易受越狱攻击的影响，这削弱了它们的安全对齐。现有的防御机制通常依赖于仅应用于最终输出的事后过滤，导致中间推理步骤未被监控，易受对抗性操控。为了解决这一问题，本文提出了一种更安全的思维链（SFCoT）框架，该框架实时主动评估和校准潜在不安全的推理步骤。SFCoT结合了三级安全评分系统和多角度一致性验证机制，旨在检测推理过程中的潜在风险。随后，动态干预模块执行针对性校准，以将推理轨迹引导向安全结果。实验结果表明，SFCoT将攻击成功率从58.97%降低到12.31%，证明其作为一种有效且高效的LLM安全增强方法，且没有显著降低整体性能。

This approach is well-motivated as it aims to enhance safety without sacrificing performance. The methodology includes a dynamic intervention module that recalibrates reasoning trajectories to ensure safer outcomes. From Evaluation to Defense: Advancing Safety in Video Large Language Models
Authors: Yiwei Sun, Peiqi Jiang, Chuanbin Liu, Luohao Lin, Zhiying Lu, Hongtao Xie
Venue: ICLR 2026
First: 2025-05-22T13:16:53+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-16T13:05:37+00:00
Comments: Accepted at ICLR 2026
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
While the safety risks of image-based large language models (Image LLMs) have been extensively studied, their video-based counterparts (Video LLMs) remain critically under-examined. To systematically study this problem, we introduce VideoSafetyEval - a large-scale, real-world benchmark for Video LLM safety, which comprises 11.4k video-query pairs and spans 19 principal risk categories. Based on this, we reveal that integrating video modality degrades safety performance by an average of 34.2%, thereby exposing systemic risks in multimodal attack exploitation. To address this vulnerability, we propose VideoSafety-R1, a dual-stage framework achieving unprecedented safety gains through three innovations: (1) the VideoSafetyThinking dataset contains 46k video-query-thinking response triplets; (2) Alarm Token-Guided Safety Fine-Tuning (AT-SFT) injects learnable alarm tokens into visual and textual sequences, enabling explicit harm perception across modalities via multitask objectives; and (3) safety-guided GRPO enhances defensive reasoning through dynamic policy optimization with rule-based rewards derived from dual-modality verification. These components synergize to shift safety alignment from harm perception to active reasoning. The framework achieves a 71.1% improvement on VSE-HH, and improves by 59.1%, 44.3%, and 15.0% on the image safety datasets MMBench, VLGuard, and FigStep, respectively. Our code and dataset are available at https://github.com/Emiya-syw/VideoSafety-R1.git. Note: This paper contains harmful language and image examples, and reader discretion is recommended.

The methodology involves the creation of the VideoSafetyThinking dataset, Alarm Token-Guided Safety Fine-Tuning, and safety-guided GRPO, which collectively improve safety performance by 71.1% on the VSE-HH task and show substantial gains on multiple image safety datasets, thus effectively supporting the goal of enhancing Video LLM safety.

OffTopicEval: When Large Language Models Enter the Wrong Chat, Almost Always!
Authors: Jingdi Lei, Varun Gumma, Rishabh Bhardwaj, Seok Min Lim, Chuan Li, Amir Zadeh, Soujanya Poria
First: 2025-09-30T16:39:17+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-13T11:01:37+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large Language Model (LLM) safety is one of the most pressing challenges for enabling wide-scale deployment. While most studies and global discussions focus on generic harms, such as models assisting users in harming themselves or others, enterprises face a more fundamental concern: whether LLM-based agents are safe for their intended use case. To address this, we introduce operational safety, defined as an LLM's ability to appropriately accept or refuse user queries when tasked with a specific purpose. We further propose OffTopicEval, an evaluation suite and benchmark for measuring operational safety both in general and within specific agentic use cases. Our evaluations on six model families comprising 20 open-weight LLMs reveal that while performance varies across models, all of them remain highly operationally unsafe. Even the strongest models - Qwen-3 (235B) with 77.77% and Mistral (24B) with 79.96% - fall far short of reliable operational safety, while GPT models plateau in the 62-73% range, Phi achieves only mid-level scores (48-70%), and Gemma and Llama-3 collapse to 39.53% and 23.84%, respectively. While operational safety is a core model alignment issue, to suppress these failures, we propose prompt-based steering methods: query grounding (Q-ground) and system-prompt grounding (P-ground), which substantially improve OOD refusal. Q-ground provides consistent gains of up to 23%, while P-ground delivers even larger boosts, raising Llama-3.3 (70B) by 41% and Qwen-3 (30B) by 27%. These results highlight both the urgent need for operational safety interventions and the promise of prompt-based steering as a first step toward more reliable LLM-based agents.
中文标题/摘要
标题：OffTopicEval：当大型语言模型进入错误的聊天时，几乎总是如此！
大型语言模型（LLM）安全性是实现大规模部署面临的最紧迫挑战之一。虽然大多数研究和全球讨论集中在一般性危害上，例如模型帮助用户伤害自己或他人，但企业面临更根本的担忧：基于LLM的代理是否安全用于其预期用途。为了解决这个问题，我们引入了操作安全性，定义为LLM在特定目的下适当地接受或拒绝用户查询的能力。我们进一步提出了OffTopicEval，一个评估套件和基准，用于测量一般和特定代理使用案例中的操作安全性。我们对六个模型家族中20个开放权重LLM的评估显示，尽管模型之间的性能差异很大，但它们的操作安全性都极低。即使是最强的模型——Qwen-3（235B）得分77.77%和Mistral（24B）得分79.96%——也远未达到可靠的操作安全性，而GPT模型的得分停留在62-73%范围内，Phi仅获得中等得分（48-70%），Gemma和Llama-3分别降至39.53%和23.84%。虽然操作安全性是核心模型对齐问题，为了抑制这些失败，我们提出了基于提示的引导方法：查询基础（Q-ground）和系统提示基础（P-ground），显著提高了OOD拒绝率。Q-ground提供了高达23%的持续增益，而P-ground则提供了更大的提升，将Llama-3.3（70B）提高了41%，将Qwen-3（30B）提高了27%。这些结果突显了对操作安全性干预的迫切需求，以及基于提示的引导作为朝着更可靠的基于LLM的代理迈出的第一步的前景。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the critical issue of operational safety in Large Language Models (LLMs), focusing on their ability to appropriately accept or refuse user queries for specific purposes, which has been largely overlooked in existing studies that emphasize generic harms. Previous methods have primarily concentrated on general safety concerns, failing to assess the models' performance in specific use cases, leading to a gap in understanding their operational reliability. This paper introduces OffTopicEval, an evaluation suite designed to measure operational safety across various LLMs, revealing that all tested models exhibit significant operational safety deficiencies, with performance metrics indicating that even the best models do not meet acceptable safety standards. The proposed methodology includes prompt-based steering techniques, specifically query grounding (Q-ground) and system-prompt grounding (P-ground), which effectively enhance out-of-distribution refusal rates, achieving performance improvements of up to 41% in certain models. These findings underscore the necessity for targeted operational safety measures and demonstrate the potential of prompt-based approaches to enhance LLM reliability.
本研究关注大型语言模型（LLM）中的操作安全性问题，特别是它们在特定目的下处理用户查询的能力。以往的研究主要集中在一般性危害上，忽视了企业在部署LLM时面临的具体安全问题。提出的OffTopicEval评估套件和基准旨在衡量各种代理使用案例中的操作安全性，结果显示所有测试模型均存在显著的操作安全性缺陷，性能指标表明即使是最佳模型也未达到可靠性标准。本文引入了基于提示的引导方法，特别是查询引导（Q-ground）和系统提示引导（P-ground），有效提高了分布外（OOD）拒绝率，某些模型的性能提升可达41%。这项研究有助于理解LLM中的操作安全性，并提出可行的方法来减轻实际应用中的安全风险。
Benchmark of Benchmarks: Unpacking Influence and Code Repository Quality in LLM Safety Benchmarks
Authors: Junjie Chu, Xinyue Shen, Ye Leng, Michael Backes, Yun Shen, Yang Zhang
First: 2026-03-03T09:10:45+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-12T11:49:16+00:00
Comments: 22 pages. 19 figures
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
The rapid growth of research in LLM safety makes it hard to track all advances. Benchmarks are therefore crucial for capturing key trends and enabling systematic comparisons. Yet, it remains unclear why certain benchmarks gain prominence, and no systematic assessment has been conducted on their academic influence or code quality. This paper fills this gap by presenting the first multi-dimensional evaluation of the influence (based on five metrics) and code quality (based on both automated and human assessment) on LLM safety benchmarks, analyzing 31 benchmarks and 382 non-benchmarks across prompt injection, jailbreak, and hallucination. We find that benchmark papers show no significant advantage in academic influence (e.g., citation count and density) over non-benchmark papers. We uncover a key misalignment: while author prominence correlates with paper influence, neither author prominence nor paper influence shows a significant correlation with code quality. Our results also indicate substantial room for improvement in code and supplementary materials: only 39% of repositories are ready-to-use, 16% include flawless installation guides, and a mere 6% address ethical considerations. Given that the work of prominent researchers tends to attract greater attention, they need to lead the effort in setting higher standards.
中文标题/摘要
标题：基准中的基准：解读LLM安全基准中的影响力和代码库质量
LLM安全研究的快速增长使得追踪所有进展变得困难。因此，基准对于捕捉关键趋势和实现系统比较至关重要。然而，尚不清楚为何某些基准会获得突出地位，也没有对其学术影响力或代码质量进行系统评估。本文通过对31个基准和382个非基准在提示注入、越狱和幻觉方面的影响（基于五个指标）和代码质量（基于自动和人工评估）进行首次多维评估，填补了这一空白。我们发现基准论文在学术影响力（例如引用次数和密度）上并未显著优于非基准论文。我们揭示了一个关键的不一致：尽管作者的知名度与论文影响力相关，但作者知名度和论文影响力与代码质量之间并没有显著相关性。我们的结果还表明代码和补充材料有很大的改进空间：只有39%的代码库是可直接使用的，16%包含无误的安装指南，只有6%涉及伦理考虑。考虑到知名研究者的工作往往吸引更多关注，他们需要在设定更高标准的努力中发挥领导作用。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the challenges in tracking advancements in LLM safety due to the rapid growth of the field and the lack of systematic assessments of benchmark influence and code quality. Previous methods did not adequately evaluate the academic influence or the quality of code associated with benchmarks, leading to a gap in understanding their prominence and effectiveness. This paper proposes a multi-dimensional evaluation framework that assesses both influence and code quality across 31 benchmarks and 382 non-benchmarks related to prompt injection, jailbreak, and hallucination. The findings reveal that benchmark papers do not significantly outperform non-benchmark papers in terms of academic influence, and there is a notable misalignment between author prominence, paper influence, and code quality. The study highlights the need for improved standards in code repositories, with only a small percentage meeting readiness and ethical guidelines, thus contributing valuable insights for future research in LLM safety.
本研究解决了由于LLM安全领域快速发展而导致的跟踪进展的挑战，强调基准在系统比较中的重要性。以往的方法缺乏对这些基准的学术影响和代码质量的系统评估，导致不清楚某些基准突出的原因。本文提出了一种多维评估框架，评估31个基准和382个非基准的影响力和代码质量，揭示基准论文在学术影响力上并未显著优于非基准论文，并且作者的突出程度与代码质量之间存在不匹配。研究结果表明，代码和补充材料的质量有很大的提升空间，只有少数符合基本的可用性和伦理标准，因此强调了知名研究者需要设定更高的基准。所采用的方法包括基于五个影响力指标的综合分析以及对代码质量的自动化和人工评估，为LLM安全基准的现状及其有效性提供了有价值的见解。
Hiding in Plain Sight: A Steganographic Approach to Stealthy LLM Jailbreaks
Authors: Jianing Geng, Biao Yi, Zekun Fei, Ruiqi He, Lihai Nie, Tong Li, Zheli Liu
First: 2025-05-22T15:07:34+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-12T10:54:29+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
Jailbreak attacks pose a serious threat to Large Language Models (LLMs) by bypassing their safety mechanisms. A truly advanced jailbreak is defined not only by its effectiveness but, more critically, by its stealthiness. However, existing methods face a fundamental trade-off between semantic stealth (hiding malicious intent) and linguistic stealth (appearing natural), leaving them vulnerable to detection. To resolve this trade-off, we propose StegoAttack, a framework that leverages steganography. The core insight is to embed a harmful query within a benign, semantically coherent paragraph. This design provides semantic stealth by concealing the existence of malicious content and ensures linguistic stealth by maintaining the natural fluency of the cover paragraph. We evaluate StegoAttack on four state-of-the-art, safety-aligned LLMs, including GPT-5 and Gemini-3, and benchmark it against eight leading jailbreak methods. Our results show that StegoAttack achieves an average attack success rate (ASR) of 95.50%, outperforming existing baselines across all four models. Critically, its ASR drops by less than 27.00% under external detectors, while maintaining natural language distribution. This demonstrates that steganography effectively decouples linguistic and semantic stealth, thereby posing a fully concealed yet highly effective security threat. The code is available at https://github.com/GenggengSvan/StegoAttack
中文标题/摘要
标题：明目张胆的隐匿：一种隐写学方法用于隐秘的LLM越狱
越狱攻击通过绕过大型语言模型（LLM）的安全机制，对其构成严重威胁。真正先进的越狱不仅以其有效性为定义，更重要的是其隐秘性。然而，现有方法在语义隐秘（隐藏恶意意图）和语言隐秘（看起来自然）之间面临根本的权衡，使其易于被检测。为了解决这一权衡，我们提出了StegoAttack，一个利用隐写学的框架。核心见解是将有害查询嵌入一个良性、语义连贯的段落中。该设计通过隐藏恶意内容的存在提供语义隐秘，并通过保持覆盖段落的自然流畅性确保语言隐秘。我们在四个最先进的、安全对齐的LLM上评估StegoAttack，包括GPT-5和Gemini-3，并与八种领先的越狱方法进行基准测试。我们的结果表明，StegoAttack在所有四个模型上实现了95.50%的平均攻击成功率（ASR），超越了现有基线。关键是，在外部检测器下，其ASR下降不到27.00%，同时保持自然语言分布。这表明隐写学有效地解耦了语言和语义隐秘，从而构成了一个完全隐蔽但高度有效的安全威胁。代码可在https://github.com/GenggengSvan/StegoAttack获取。
Summary / 总结
This article addresses the growing concern of jailbreak attacks on Large Language Models (LLMs), which threaten their safety mechanisms by bypassing them. Previous methods struggle with a trade-off between semantic stealth, which hides malicious intent, and linguistic stealth, which ensures natural language use, making them susceptible to detection. The proposed approach, StegoAttack, utilizes steganography to embed harmful queries within benign paragraphs, effectively resolving this trade-off by providing both semantic and linguistic stealth. The contribution of this paper lies in demonstrating that steganography can decouple these two forms of stealth, achieving an average attack success rate of 95.50% across four advanced LLMs, including GPT-5 and Gemini-3, while maintaining a low drop in performance under external detection. This indicates that the method not only meets its goals but also poses a significant security challenge to existing systems.
本研究针对大型语言模型（LLM）面临的越狱攻击威胁，该攻击可以绕过安全机制。以往的方法在语义隐蔽性（隐藏恶意意图）和语言隐蔽性（保持自然语言使用）之间存在权衡，使其易于被检测。提出的StegoAttack框架利用隐写术将有害查询嵌入无害段落中，有效实现了两种隐蔽性。本文的贡献在于提出了一种新颖的方法，攻击成功率显著提高，在包括GPT-5和Gemini-3在内的四个先进LLM上平均达到95.50%，同时在外部检测下性能下降不到27.00%。这表明所提出的方法成功解决了现有技术的局限性，并构成了一个隐蔽而有效的安全威胁。
ADVERSA: Measuring Multi-Turn Guardrail Degradation and Judge Reliability in Large Language Models
Authors: Harry Owiredu-Ashley
First: 2026-03-10T03:00:34+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-10T03:00:34+00:00
Comments: 12 pages, 12 figures. Independent research. Code and artifacts: https://github.com/Harry-Ashley/adversa-guardrail-degradation
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
Most adversarial evaluations of large language model (LLM) safety assess single prompts and report binary pass/fail outcomes, which fails to capture how safety properties evolve under sustained adversarial interaction. We present ADVERSA, an automated red-teaming framework that measures guardrail degradation dynamics as continuous per-round compliance trajectories rather than discrete jailbreak events. ADVERSA uses a fine-tuned 70B attacker model (ADVERSA-Red, Llama-3.1-70B-Instruct with QLoRA) that eliminates the attacker-side safety refusals that render off-the-shelf models unreliable as attackers, scoring victim responses on a structured 5-point rubric that treats partial compliance as a distinct measurable state. We report a controlled experiment across three frontier victim models (Claude Opus 4.6, Gemini 3.1 Pro, GPT-5.2) using a triple-judge consensus architecture in which judge reliability is measured as a first-class research outcome rather than assumed. Across 15 conversations of up to 10 adversarial rounds, we observe a 26.7% jailbreak rate with an average jailbreak round of 1.25, suggesting that in this evaluation setting, successful jailbreaks were concentrated in early rounds rather than accumulating through sustained pressure. We document inter-judge agreement rates, self-judge scoring tendencies, attacker drift as a failure mode in fine-tuned attackers deployed out of their training distribution, and attacker refusals as a previously-underreported confound in victim resistance measurement. All limitations are stated explicitly. Attack prompts are withheld per responsible disclosure policy; all other experimental artifacts are released.
中文标题/摘要
标题：ADVERSA：测量大型语言模型中的多轮护栏退化和评审可靠性
大多数对大型语言模型（LLM）安全性的对抗性评估评估单个提示并报告二元通过/失败结果，这未能捕捉安全属性在持续对抗交互下的演变。我们提出了ADVERSA，一个自动化红队框架，测量护栏退化动态，作为连续的每轮合规轨迹，而不是离散的越狱事件。ADVERSA使用经过微调的70B攻击者模型（ADVERSA-Red，Llama-3.1-70B-Instruct与QLoRA），消除了攻击者侧的安全拒绝，使现成模型在攻击者中不可靠，使用结构化的5分制评分受害者响应，将部分合规视为一个独特的可测量状态。我们报告了在三个前沿受害者模型（Claude Opus 4.6，Gemini 3.1 Pro，GPT-5.2）中进行的受控实验，使用三重评审共识架构，其中评审可靠性被视为一项一流的研究结果，而不是假设。在15次对话中，最多进行10轮对抗，我们观察到26.7%的越狱率，平均越狱轮次为1.25，这表明在该评估环境中，成功的越狱集中在早期轮次，而不是通过持续压力积累。我们记录了评审间一致性率、自我评审评分倾向、在训练分布外部署的微调攻击者中的攻击者漂移作为失败模式，以及攻击者拒绝作为受害者抵抗测量中之前未报告的混淆因素。所有限制均明确说明。攻击提示根据负责任的披露政策被保留；所有其他实验材料均已发布。
Summary / 总结
This research addresses the limitations of existing adversarial evaluations of large language models (LLMs), which typically assess safety through single prompts and binary outcomes, failing to capture the dynamics of safety properties during prolonged adversarial interactions. The proposed ADVERSA framework introduces a continuous measurement approach for guardrail degradation, utilizing a fine-tuned 70B attacker model that mitigates reliability issues seen in off-the-shelf models. The contribution of this paper lies in its novel methodology that employs a triple-judge consensus architecture to evaluate judge reliability as a key outcome, revealing a 26.7% jailbreak rate across 15 conversations with an average of 1.25 jailbreak rounds, indicating that vulnerabilities are more prevalent in early interactions. This approach not only enhances the understanding of model safety under sustained pressure but also provides a structured rubric for assessing compliance, thereby supporting the goals of improving LLM safety assessments.
本研究解决了现有大型语言模型（LLM）对抗性评估的局限性，这些评估通常通过单一提示和二元结果来评估安全性，未能捕捉在持续对抗交互中安全属性的动态变化。提出的ADVERSA框架引入了一种连续测量护栏降解的方法，利用经过微调的70B攻击者模型，减轻了现成模型中存在的可靠性问题。该研究的贡献在于采用三重评审共识架构，将评审可靠性作为关键结果进行评估，揭示了在15次对话中26.7%的越狱率，平均每轮越狱次数为1.25，表明成功的越狱往往发生在早期，而不是通过持续压力累积。该方法增强了对LLM中对抗性交互的理解，并提供了一个结构化的合规性测量标准，从而有效支持了研究目标。
Beyond Benchmarks: Dynamic, Automatic And Systematic Red-Teaming Agents For Trustworthy Medical Language Models
Authors: Jiazhen Pan, Bailiang Jian, Paul Hager, Yundi Zhang, Che Liu, Friedrike Jungmann, Hongwei Bran Li, Chenyu You, Junde Wu, Jiayuan Zhu, Fenglin Liu, Yuyuan Liu, Niklas Bubeck, Christian Wachinger, Chen, Chen, Zhenyu Gong, Cheng Ouyang, Georgios Kaissis, Benedikt Wiestler, Daniel Rueckert
First: 2025-07-30T08:44:22+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-09T15:37:01+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Ensuring the safety and reliability of large language models (LLMs) in clinical practice is critical to prevent patient harm. However, LLMs are advancing so rapidly that static benchmarks quickly become obsolete or prone to overfitting, yielding a misleading picture of model trustworthiness. Here we introduce a Dynamic, Automatic, and Systematic (DAS) red-teaming framework that continuously stress-tests LLMs across four safety-critical axes: robustness, privacy, bias/fairness, and hallucination. Validated against board-certified clinicians with high concordance, a suite of adversarial agents autonomously mutates clinical test cases to uncover vulnerabilities in real time. Applying DAS to 15 proprietary and open-source LLMs revealed a profound gap between high static benchmark performance and low dynamic reliability - the ``Benchmarking Gap''. Despite median MedQA accuracy exceeding 80\%, 94\% of previously correct answers failed our dynamic robustness tests. Crucially, this brittleness generalized to the realistic, open-ended HealthBench dataset, where top-tier models exhibited failure rates exceeding 70\% and stark shifts in model rankings across evaluations, suggesting that high scores on established static benchmarks may reflect superficial memorization. We observed similarly high failure rates across other domains: privacy leaks were elicited in 86\% of scenarios, cognitive-bias priming altered clinical recommendations in 81\% of fairness tests, and we identified hallucination rates exceeding 74\% in widely used models. By converting medical LLM safety analysis from a static checklist into a dynamic stress-test, DAS provides a foundational, scalable, and living platform to surface the latent risks that must be addressed before the next generation of medical AI can be safely deployed.
中文标题/摘要
标题：超越基准：动态、自动和系统化的红队代理用于可信的医疗语言模型
确保大型语言模型（LLMs）在临床实践中的安全性和可靠性对于防止患者伤害至关重要。然而，LLMs的发展速度如此之快，以至于静态基准很快变得过时或容易过拟合，从而产生误导性的模型可信度图景。在此，我们介绍了一种动态、自动和系统化（DAS）红队框架，持续对LLMs在四个安全关键轴上进行压力测试：鲁棒性、隐私、公平性/偏见和幻觉。经过与高一致性的董事会认证临床医生的验证，一套对抗性代理自主变更临床测试案例，以实时发现漏洞。将DAS应用于15个专有和开源LLMs揭示了高静态基准性能与低动态可靠性之间的深刻差距——“基准差距”。尽管中位数MedQA准确率超过80%，94%的先前正确答案未能通过我们的动态鲁棒性测试。至关重要的是，这种脆弱性在现实的开放式HealthBench数据集中得到了普遍体现，顶级模型的失败率超过70%，并且在评估中模型排名发生了显著变化，这表明在既定静态基准上获得的高分可能反映了表面的记忆。我们在其他领域也观察到了类似的高失败率：在86%的场景中引发了隐私泄露，81%的公平性测试中认知偏见的引导改变了临床建议，并且我们在广泛使用的模型中发现幻觉率超过74%。通过将医疗LLM安全分析从静态检查表转变为动态压力测试，DAS提供了一个基础的、可扩展的和动态的平台，以揭示必须在下一代医疗AI安全部署之前解决的潜在风险。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the critical need for ensuring the safety and reliability of large language models (LLMs) in clinical practice, as traditional static benchmarks quickly become outdated and can misrepresent model trustworthiness. Previous methods often relied on fixed evaluations that failed to capture real-time vulnerabilities, leading to misleading assessments of model performance. The proposed Dynamic, Automatic, and Systematic (DAS) red-teaming framework overcomes these limitations by continuously stress-testing LLMs across key safety dimensions, including robustness, privacy, bias/fairness, and hallucination. This methodology involves autonomous mutation of clinical test cases validated against board-certified clinicians, revealing a significant 'Benchmarking Gap' where high static performance does not correlate with dynamic reliability. The study found that while median MedQA accuracy was over 80%, 94% of previously correct answers failed dynamic robustness tests, and failure rates exceeded 70% on the HealthBench dataset, highlighting the superficial nature of static benchmarks and the urgent need for dynamic evaluation methods in medical AI.
本研究解决了临床环境中对可靠的大型语言模型（LLMs）的迫切需求，因为传统的静态基准很快就会过时，并可能误导模型的可信度。以往的方法依赖于固定的评估，常常导致过拟合，未能捕捉实时的脆弱性，而提出的动态、自动和系统化（DAS）红队框架则持续对LLMs在关键安全维度（如稳健性、隐私、公平性和幻觉）进行压力测试。本文的贡献在于揭示了“基准差距”，即高静态基准分数与动态可靠性之间并无关联，94%的先前正确答案在动态稳健性测试中失败。该方法论涉及使用对抗性代理自动变更临床测试案例，导致显著发现，显示在HealthBench数据集上的失败率超过70%，隐私泄露和认知偏见的高发生率，表明现有基准可能不足以确保医疗AI应用的安全性。
Automating Deception: Scalable Multi-Turn LLM Jailbreaks
Authors: Adarsh Kumarappan, Ananya Mujoo
First: 2025-11-24T03:15:11+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-07T08:41:48+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Multi-turn conversational attacks, which leverage psychological principles like Foot-in-the-Door (FITD), where a small initial request paves the way for a more significant one, to bypass safety alignments, pose a persistent threat to Large Language Models (LLMs). Progress in defending against these attacks is hindered by a reliance on manual, hard-to-scale dataset creation. This paper introduces a novel, automated pipeline for generating large-scale, psychologically-grounded multi-turn jailbreak datasets. We systematically operationalize FITD techniques into reproducible templates, creating a benchmark of 1,500 scenarios across illegal activities and offensive content. We evaluate seven models from three major LLM families under both multi-turn (with history) and single-turn (without history) conditions. Our results reveal stark differences in contextual robustness: models in the GPT family demonstrate a significant vulnerability to conversational history, with Attack Success Rates (ASR) increasing by as much as 32 percentage points. In contrast, Google's Gemini 2.5 Flash exhibits exceptional resilience, proving nearly immune to these attacks, while Anthropic's Claude 3 Haiku shows strong but imperfect resistance. These findings highlight a critical divergence in how current safety architectures handle conversational context and underscore the need for defenses that can resist narrative-based manipulation.
中文标题/摘要
标题：自动化欺骗：可扩展的多轮LLM越狱
多轮对话攻击利用心理学原理，如“脚踏实地”（FITD），通过小的初始请求为更大的请求铺平道路，以绕过安全对齐，对大型语言模型（LLM）构成持续威胁。防御这些攻击的进展受到依赖于手动、难以扩展的数据集创建的阻碍。本文介绍了一种新颖的自动化管道，用于生成大规模、基于心理学的多轮越狱数据集。我们系统地将FITD技术操作化为可重复的模板，创建了一个涵盖非法活动和攻击性内容的1,500个场景的基准。我们在多轮（带历史）和单轮（无历史）条件下评估了来自三个主要LLM家族的七个模型。我们的结果揭示了上下文鲁棒性方面的显著差异：GPT家族的模型对对话历史表现出显著脆弱性，攻击成功率（ASR）增加了多达32个百分点。相比之下，谷歌的Gemini 2.5 Flash表现出卓越的韧性，几乎对这些攻击免疫，而Anthropic的Claude 3 Haiku则显示出强但不完美的抵抗力。这些发现突显了当前安全架构在处理对话上下文方面的关键分歧，并强调了需要能够抵御叙事操控的防御措施。
Summary / 总结
This article addresses the ongoing threat posed by multi-turn conversational attacks on Large Language Models (LLMs), which exploit psychological principles like the Foot-in-the-Door (FITD) technique to bypass safety measures. Previous methods have relied on manual dataset creation, which is not scalable and limits the effectiveness of defenses against such attacks. The proposed approach automates the generation of large-scale, psychologically-informed multi-turn jailbreak datasets, operationalizing FITD techniques into reproducible templates and creating a benchmark of 1,500 scenarios. The research methodology involves evaluating seven models from three major LLM families under both multi-turn and single-turn conditions, revealing that GPT models are particularly vulnerable to conversational history, while Google's Gemini 2.5 Flash shows remarkable resilience. These findings contribute to a better understanding of how different safety architectures respond to conversational context and highlight the necessity for improved defenses against narrative-based manipulation.
本文探讨了多轮对话攻击对大型语言模型（LLMs）日益增长的威胁，这些攻击利用心理学原理，如脚踏实地（FITD）技术，绕过安全措施。以往的方法依赖于手动创建数据集，这种方式难以扩展，限制了对这些攻击的有效防御。提出的方法自动生成大规模、基于心理学的多轮越狱数据集，将FITD技术操作化为可重复的模板，并创建了1500个场景的基准。研究方法涉及在多轮和单轮条件下评估来自三个主要LLM家族的七个模型，结果显示GPT模型对对话历史特别脆弱，攻击成功率显著提高，而谷歌的Gemini 2.5 Flash表现出显著的抗攻击能力。这些贡献强调了改善对LLMs中叙事操控的防御的必要性。
Peak + Accumulation: A Proxy-Level Scoring Formula for Multi-Turn LLM Attack Detection
Authors: J Alex Corll
First: 2026-02-11T17:53:41+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-05T22:25:18+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Multi-turn prompt injection attacks distribute malicious intent across multiple conversation turns, exploiting the assumption that each turn is evaluated independently. While single-turn detection has been extensively studied, no published formula exists for aggregating per-turn pattern scores into a conversation-level risk score at the proxy layer -- without invoking an LLM. We identify a fundamental flaw in the intuitive weighted-average approach: it converges to the per-turn score regardless of turn count, meaning a 20-turn persistent attack scores identically to a single suspicious turn. Drawing on analogies from change-point detection (CUSUM), Bayesian belief updating, and security risk-based alerting, we propose peak + accumulation scoring -- a formula combining peak single-turn risk, persistence ratio, and category diversity. Evaluated on 10,654 multi-turn conversations -- 588 attacks sourced from WildJailbreak adversarial prompts and 10,066 benign conversations from WildChat -- the formula achieves 90.8% recall at 1.20% false positive rate with an F1 of 85.9%. A sensitivity analysis over the persistence parameter reveals a phase transition at rho ~ 0.4, where recall jumps 12 percentage points with negligible FPR increase. We release the scoring algorithm, pattern library, and evaluation harness as open source.
中文标题/摘要
标题：峰值 + 累积：一种用于多轮 LLM 攻击检测的代理级评分公式
多轮提示注入攻击在多个对话轮次中分散恶意意图，利用每个轮次独立评估的假设。尽管单轮检测已被广泛研究，但在代理层中没有已发布的公式用于将每轮模式分数聚合为对话级风险分数，而不调用 LLM。我们识别出直观加权平均方法的一个根本缺陷：无论轮次数量如何，它都收敛于每轮分数，这意味着 20 轮持续攻击的得分与单个可疑轮次相同。借鉴变点检测（CUSUM）、贝叶斯信念更新和基于安全风险的警报，我们提出了峰值 + 累积评分——一个结合峰值单轮风险、持续比率和类别多样性的公式。在 10,654 个多轮对话中进行评估——588 个攻击源自 WildJailbreak 对抗提示，10,066 个良性对话来自 WildChat——该公式在 1.20% 的假阳性率下实现了 90.8% 的召回率，F1 值为 85.9%。对持续参数的敏感性分析显示在 rho ~ 0.4 处发生相变，召回率跃升 12 个百分点，假阳性率增加微乎其微。我们将评分算法、模式库和评估工具作为开源发布。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the challenge of detecting multi-turn prompt injection attacks in conversational AI, which exploit the assumption of independent evaluation of each turn. Previous methods primarily focused on single-turn detection, lacking a comprehensive formula to aggregate per-turn scores into a conversation-level risk score, leading to ineffective detection of persistent attacks. This paper introduces a novel peak + accumulation scoring formula that combines peak single-turn risk, persistence ratio, and category diversity, effectively overcoming the limitations of existing methods. The proposed methodology was evaluated on a dataset of 10,654 multi-turn conversations, achieving a recall of 90.8% at a 1.20% false positive rate and an F1 score of 85.9%, demonstrating its effectiveness in detecting multi-turn attacks and supporting the research goals. The authors also provide the scoring algorithm, pattern library, and evaluation harness as open source resources.

Safety Guardrails for LLM-Enabled Robots
Authors: Zachary Ravichandran, Alexander Robey, Vijay Kumar, George J. Pappas, Hamed Hassani
First: 2025-03-10T22:01:56+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-03T23:39:07+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Project1
Abstract
Although the integration of large language models (LLMs) into robotics has unlocked transformative capabilities, it has also introduced significant safety concerns, ranging from average-case LLM errors (e.g., hallucinations) to adversarial jailbreaking attacks, which can produce harmful robot behavior in real-world settings. Traditional robot safety approaches do not address the contextual vulnerabilities of LLMs, and current LLM safety approaches overlook the physical risks posed by robots operating in real-world environments. To ensure the safety of LLM-enabled robots, we propose RoboGuard, a two-stage guardrail architecture. RoboGuard first contextualizes pre-defined safety rules by grounding them in the robot's environment using a root-of-trust LLM. This LLM is shielded from malicious prompts and employs chain-of-thought (CoT) reasoning to generate context-dependent safety specifications, such as temporal logic constraints. RoboGuard then resolves conflicts between these contextual safety specifications and potentially unsafe plans using temporal logic control synthesis, ensuring compliance while minimally violating user preferences. In simulation and real-world experiments that consider worst-case jailbreaking attacks, RoboGuard reduces the execution of unsafe plans from over 92% to below 3% without compromising performance on safe plans. We also demonstrate that RoboGuard is resource-efficient, robust against adaptive attacks, and enhanced by its root-of-trust LLM's CoT reasoning. These results demonstrate the potential of RoboGuard to mitigate the safety risks and enhance the reliability of LLM-enabled robots. We provide additional resources at https://robo-guard.github.io/.
中文标题/摘要

Toward a Dynamic Stackelberg Game-Theoretic Framework for Agentic AI Defense Against LLM Jailbreaking
Authors: Zhengye Han, Quanyan Zhu
Venue: ICLR 2026
First: 2025-07-10T22:37:47+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-02T23:19:02+00:00
Comments: Accepted to ICLR 2026 AIMS Workshop. 13 pages, 3 figures
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
This paper proposes a game theoretic framework that models the interaction between prompt engineers and large language models (LLMs) as a two player extensive form game coupled with a Rapidly exploring Random Trees (RRT) search over prompt space. The attacker incrementally samples, extends, and tests prompts, while the LLM chooses to accept, reject, or redirect, leading to terminal outcomes of Safe Interaction, Blocked, or Jailbreak. Embedding RRT exploration inside the extensive form game captures both the discovery phase of jailbreak strategies and the strategic responses of the model. Furthermore, we show that the defender behavior can be interpreted through a local Stackelberg equilibrium condition, which explains when the attacker can no longer obtain profitable prompt deviations and provides a theoretical lens for understanding the effectiveness of our Purple Agent defense. The resulting game tree thus offers a principled foundation for evaluating, interpreting, and hardening LLM guardrails.
中文标题/摘要
标题：面向动态斯塔克尔伯格博弈理论框架的代理人工智能防御大语言模型越狱
本文提出了一个博弈理论框架，模拟提示工程师与大语言模型（LLMs）之间的互动，作为一个两人广泛形式的博弈，并结合在提示空间上的快速探索随机树（RRT）搜索。攻击者逐步采样、扩展和测试提示，而LLM选择接受、拒绝或重定向，导致安全互动、被阻止或越狱的终局结果。将RRT探索嵌入广泛形式的博弈中，捕捉了越狱策略的发现阶段和模型的战略响应。此外，我们展示了防御者行为可以通过局部斯塔克尔伯格均衡条件进行解释，这解释了攻击者何时无法再获得有利的提示偏差，并为理解我们紫色代理防御的有效性提供了理论视角。因此，所得到的博弈树为评估、解释和强化LLM保护措施提供了原则基础。
Summary / 总结

The proposed approach introduces a game theoretic framework that treats the interaction as a two-player extensive form game, incorporating Rapidly exploring Random Trees (RRT) to explore prompt space effectively. This method not only captures the dynamics of prompt sampling and testing by attackers but also provides insights into the defender's strategies through a local Stackelberg equilibrium. The contribution of this paper lies in its principled foundation for evaluating and enhancing LLM defenses, demonstrating that the proposed framework can lead to improved outcomes in terms of safe interactions and reduced jailbreak success rates.

Enhancing Safety of Large Language Models via Embedding Space Separation
Authors: Xu Zhao, Xiting Wang, Weiran Shen
First: 2026-03-01T07:22:38+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-01T07:22:38+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) have achieved impressive capabilities, yet ensuring their safety against harmful prompts remains a critical challenge. Recent work has revealed that the latent representations (embeddings) of harmful and safe queries in LLMs typically exhibit linear separability, a property that has been exploited to construct attacks by perturbing the embeddings of harmful queries towards the safe subspace. Motivated by this observation, we propose a representation-level fine-tuning approach, named Embedding Space Separation (ES2), which improves LLM safety by explicitly enlarging the distance between harmful and safe representations in the embedding space. To prevent degradation of model's general capabilities, we introduce a Kullback-Leibler (KL) divergence regularization term into the loss function, which constrains the logits of the fine-tuned model to align with those of the original base model on harmless inputs. We evaluate our method on several open-source LLMs using standard safety benchmarks. Extensive experimental results demonstrate that our approach substantially improves model safety while maintaining comparable general capabilities.
中文标题/摘要

大型语言模型（LLMs）已实现令人印象深刻的能力，但确保其对有害提示的安全性仍然是一个关键挑战。最近的研究表明，LLMs中有害和安全查询的潜在表示（嵌入）通常表现出线性可分性，这一特性已被利用，通过扰动有害查询的嵌入朝向安全子空间来构建攻击。基于这一观察，我们提出了一种名为嵌入空间分离（ES2）的表示级微调方法，通过明确增大嵌入空间中有害和安全表示之间的距离来提高LLM的安全性。为了防止模型一般能力的退化，我们在损失函数中引入了Kullback-Leibler（KL）散度正则化项，约束微调模型的logits与原始基础模型在无害输入上的对齐。我们在多个开源LLMs上使用标准安全基准评估我们的方法。大量实验结果表明，我们的方法显著提高了模型的安全性，同时保持了可比的通用能力。

CourtGuard: A Model-Agnostic Framework for Zero-Shot Policy Adaptation in LLM Safety
Authors: Umid Suleymanov, Rufiz Bayramov, Suad Gafarli, Seljan Musayeva, Taghi Mammadov, Aynur Akhundlu, Murat Kantarcioglu
First: 2026-02-26T02:52:11+00:00 · Latest: 2026-02-26T02:52:11+00:00
Comments: Under Review
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Current safety mechanisms for Large Language Models (LLMs) rely heavily on static, fine-tuned classifiers that suffer from adaptation rigidity, the inability to enforce new governance rules without expensive retraining. To address this, we introduce CourtGuard, a retrieval-augmented multi-agent framework that reimagines safety evaluation as Evidentiary Debate. By orchestrating an adversarial debate grounded in external policy documents, CourtGuard achieves state-of-the-art performance across 7 safety benchmarks, outperforming dedicated policy-following baselines without fine-tuning. Beyond standard metrics, we highlight two critical capabilities: (1) Zero-Shot Adaptability, where our framework successfully generalized to an out-of-domain Wikipedia Vandalism task (achieving 90\% accuracy) by swapping the reference policy; and (2) Automated Data Curation and Auditing, where we leveraged CourtGuard to curate and audit nine novel datasets of sophisticated adversarial attacks. Our results demonstrate that decoupling safety logic from model weights offers a robust, interpretable, and adaptable path for meeting current and future regulatory requirements in AI governance.

标题：CourtGuard：一种与模型无关的零-shot策略适应框架，用于大型语言模型安全性
当前大型语言模型（LLMs）的安全机制严重依赖于静态的、微调的分类器，这些分类器存在适应性僵化的问题，无法在不进行昂贵的再训练的情况下执行新的治理规则。为了解决这个问题，我们引入了CourtGuard，这是一种增强检索的多智能体框架，将安全评估重新构想为证据辩论。通过协调基于外部政策文件的对抗性辩论，CourtGuard在7个安全基准测试中实现了最先进的性能，超越了专门的政策遵循基线而无需微调。除了标准指标外，我们强调了两个关键能力：（1）零-shot适应性，我们的框架成功地推广到一个域外的维基百科破坏任务（实现90%的准确率），通过更换参考政策；（2）自动数据策划和审计，我们利用CourtGuard策划和审计了九个新颖的复杂对抗攻击数据集。我们的结果表明，将安全逻辑与模型权重解耦为满足当前和未来AI治理监管要求提供了一条稳健、可解释和可适应的路径。
